Jamison Brereton

181
As╠Бvins
Agastya Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
9 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Although not at the same degree of difficulty as AgastyaтАЩs immediately preceding hymn to the A┼Ыvins, this one certainly has its share of puzzlesтАФthough, as so often, it restricts itself almost entirely to the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ journey to the sacrifice and the sacri fice itself. The hymn begins at the sacrifice, with the A┼Ыvins acting as priests (vs. 1), but then draws back temporally to the usual invitation to travel to the sacrifice (vss. 2тАУ3). Verse 4 gives us a tantalizing glimpse of a potential differentiation between the two A┼Ыvins, who are otherwise almost always treated as identical and identically functioning twins.
Verses 5тАУ6 are entirely parallel to each other in structure and return to the jour ney theme, but introduce another, though unnamed, figure by way of a slippery use of the word any├б тАЬother.тАЭ In verse 4 paired any├бтАЩs referred to the two individual A┼Ыvins, but in the following two verses, each containing an any├б in p─Бda c, the A┼Ыvins are jointly established in the first half of the verse and implicitly contrast with the unidentified тАЬotherтАЭ of p─Бda c. In our opinion this тАЬotherтАЭ must be Indra, identifiable because of the pair of fallow bay horses in 5c, a pair of horses that are uniquely IndraтАЩs in the R╠еgveda. It is not surprising that the A┼Ыvins and Indra should be journeying at the same time, since both are recipients of parts of the Morning Pressing.
The final verses (7тАУ9) take place on the sacrificial ground. Verse 8 is especially rich in striking images of the ritual: the sacrificial fire is depicted as a тАЬgleaming waspтАЭ whose sound is likened to a praise hymn, and the imminent mixing of soma and milk gives rise to a complex erotic image, with the soma a swollen тАЬbullish cloudтАЭ at the тАЬpouring outтАЭ (se╠Бka) of the milkтАФits swelling attributed to its sexual excitement at the тАЬinseminationтАЭ (se╠Бka) of the cow. In general, swelling as a sign of abundance is a consistent theme in the latter part of the hymn (vss. 5c, 6c, 8b, 8c).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen, beloved (A┼Ыvins), do you bear aloft (the materials) of food and riches, that, desirous of the sacrifice, you may send down the rain; this sacrifice offers you adoration, givers of riches, protectors of men.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

What (portion) of nourishments and riches (do) you two dearest ones (draw up), when, acting as Adhvaryus, you draw up (a portion) of the waters?
This sacrifice here has made its own encomium for you, o you
depositories of goods, helpers of the peoples.384 I.182

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd du (un)nin─лth├бс╕е, with primary ending, is formally problematic. It is tentatively assigned to a redupl. pres. by Whitney, but there is otherwise no evidence for such a pres., while the pf. is well established. Macdonell (oddly) calls it a pf.

subjunctive, but the mood sign of the subjunctive is absent. It canтАЩt be an example of simple avoidance of a paradigmatically shaky form, as in the case of *avс╣Ыс╣З─Бth─Бm in the preceding hymn (I.180.4), because the expected pf. indic. ninyathuс╕е is actually attested, with the same preverb (├║d) and the A┼Ыvins also as subject (I.116.8, 24). K├╝mmel suggests (280-81) that the form is aiming to be an injunctive (that is, I assume, an unaugmented pluperfect) meant to be distinguished from a putative imperative

*nin─лt├бm with 2ndary ending, and therefore it takes a primary ending (a solution endorsed by Witzel Got┼Н). This seems needlessly complex and, pace Hoffmann (Injunc., 111), I find the notion that an injunctive would adopt primary endings for this purpose somewhat bizarre, since secondary endings are what define the injunctive. A simpler solution is to assume the form is a nonce present generated to ambiguous perfect forms like opt. nin─лy─Бt (2x).

How to construe the genitives iс╣г─Б╠Бс╣Г ray─лс╣З─Б╠Бm and ap─Б╠Бm is another problem. I take them as parallel partitive genitives, roughly flg. Oldenberg, rather than taking the former pair as dependent on pr├йс╣гс╣нс╕еau and the latter as a pseudo-ablative as Geldner does.

Griffith

WHAT, dearest Pair, is this in strength and riches that ye as Priests are bring from the waters?
This sacrifice is your glorification, ye who protect mankind and give them treasures.

Geldner

Was war es, das ihr, die gr├╢├Яten Liebhaber von Speisegen├╝ssen, von Reicht├╝mern, den Opferdienst besorgend aus dem Wasser gesch├╢pft habt? Dieses Opfer hat euch Ehre gemacht, ihr Schatzhalter, ihr Helfer der Menschen.

Grassmann

Was ist’s, o liebste, was ihr aus den Wassern an Trunk und Reichthum dienstbeflissen herf├╝hrt? Dies Opfer hat euch hohen Ruhm bereitet, Schatzkammern ihr und Sch├╝tzer aller Menschen!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins, excellent and steady, may your chariot, vast as the earth, broad-fronted, rapid as the rain (fleet) as thought, cumulative and adorable, come hither for (our) good.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Emulative: ahamp┼лrvaс╕е, I first, is normally related to a warrior, one who would be first in battle; here, it is explained as intelligent, manasvin; or very genitive rous atyud─Бraс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Your chariot with its glossy chariot-box should come here like a
forward-coursing stream, for good faringтАФ
(the chariot) that is worthy of the sacrifice and swifter than mind,
(saying) тАЬI am in front,тАЭ o you mounters of the bull [=chariot], you
holy ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The adjectival descriptor of the chariot ahamp┼лrv├бс╕е is transparently derived from a nominal clause тАЬI am in front / IтАЩm ahead,тАЭ however unlikely this may be as the utterance of a chariot.

The second hemistich consists entirely of a nominal relative clause referring to the chariot, with two vocatives, the phrasal vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зa sth─Бt─Бr─Б тАЬyou mounters of the bullтАЭ in initial position and dhiс╣гс╣Зi y─Б near the end. The latter is commonly used of the A┼Ыvins (see, e.g., I.182.1c, 2a, in the next hymn). Here the voc. is followed by the rel.

pronoun y├бс╕е, which ends the clause. This is a remarkably odd position for a rel.

pronoun, and since this supposed rel. cl. consists of nominative qualifiers of the subject of the main clause, r├бthaс╕е, it need not have been a relative clause at all: the whole of the vs. could simply be a main clause. I think the y├бс╕е got stuck pleonastically+++(=redundant)+++ on the end of this p─Бda to provide a monosyllable to make a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence. (Cf. VI.63.6, a Triс╣гс╣нubh that ends dhiс╣гс╣Зi y─Б v─Бm, likewise with a final monosyllable.) No harm is done by this last-ditch conversion of the string of epithets in cd into a nominal rel. clause, but it is a metrically driven afterthought in my opinion. It should certainly not be taken as a standard ex. of rel. cl. word order.

The phrase m├бnaso j├бv─лy─Бn is an analytic version of manoj┼л╠Б- in 2c, there applied to the horses, not the chariot.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBorn here (in the middle region) and here (in the upper region), you are glorified together, as faultless in your forms and (perfect in) your own many excellences; one (of you) the victorious son (of the firmament), the devout (promoter) of sacred sacrifice, the other, the auspicious son of heaven, (each) upholds (the world).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Born here and here: iheha j─Бt─Б = liс╣н, born here and here, iha iha; the amplification identifies the A┼Ыvins with the sun and the moon; faultless in your forms: arepas─Б tanv─Б n─Бmabhiс╕е svaiс╕е: arepas─Б = free from sin, ap─Бpau; the allusion is to the legend of the decapitation of Dadhya├▒c, by which act, with reference to its result, no sin was incurred; the auspicious son of heaven: as the same with the moon and sun, one A┼Ыvin may be termed the son of the middle region or firmament; the other, the son of the upper region, heaven or sky

Jamison Brereton

Born (one) here, (one) there, the two have always bellowed together with (one) flawless body but with their own (multiple) names.
One of you is lauded as the victorious patron of the good battler, the other as the son of heaven dispensing a good portion.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Yet another troublesome dual verb form: av─Бva┼Ы─лt─Бm. It is generally agreed (Wh Rts, Geldner [more or less], Renou, Witzel Got┼Н, Schaeffer [179-82], K├╝mmel [486-88]) that it belongs to the root тИЪv─Б┼Ы тАШbellowтАЩ. (Grassmann assigns it to both тИЪva┼Ы тАШwishтАЩ and тИЪv─Б┼Ы without comment; for reff. to further lit. on this form see Schaeffer 181-82, K├╝mmel 487- 88.) But forms to that redupl. stem are overwhelmingly middle, while this form is active. Whether it is assigned to the intensive (Schaef.) or the pluperfect (K├╝mmel), we should expect a medial 3rd du. with secondary ending. However, as was already noted with regard to avс╣Ыс╣З─лtam in the immediately preceding hymn (I.180.4), athematic 2nd and 3rd medial duals are simply not attested, and in that case the 2nd du. active form was substituted. I think the same thing happened here, and there is therefore no reason to construct specifically active semantics for this form, as do Witzel Got┼Н.

Geldner (fld. by Renou and Witzel Got┼Н) supplies putr├бс╕е with c as well as d and also takes s├║makha- as a PN, hence тАЬ(the son) of Sumakha.тАЭ These two decisions lead to the interpretation that one of the A┼Ыvins is of human origin, the other divine. So, most clearly, Renou: тАЬDissociation inattendue des A┼Ыvins, lтАЩun dтАЩorigine humaine, lтАЩautre divine.тАЭ This is a major and unnecessary interpretive leap, and based on dubious though not impossible analyses of two details: there is no syntactic or rhetorical reason to supply putr├бс╕е in c, and s├║makha- is ordinarily an epithet of gods; acdg. to Mayrhofer (PN 102) this is the only possible passage in which it would be a personal name and would refer to a human, not a god. Although this vs. does, unusually, distinguish between the two A┼Ыvins, I see no reason to ascribe human origin to one of them on the basis of this passage, which is more naturally interpreted in another fashion. It should be noted that Geldner expresses some doubt about his interpr. in his n.

4c.

Griffith

Here sprung to life, they both have sung together, with bodies free from stain, with signs that mark them;
One of you Prince of Sacrifice, the Victor, the other counts as Heaven’s auspicious offspring.

Geldner

An verschiedenen Orten geboren stimmten die Makellosen an K├╢rper und mit ihren Namen zueinander. Der eine von euch, der sieghafte Lohnherr, gilt als Sohn des Sumakha, der andere als der beliebte Sohn des Himmels.

Grassmann

Sie, hier und dort geboren, rauschten beide vereint, an Leibern rein, nach ihrer Weise; Ein F├╝rst der eine, siegreich ├╝ber Helden, der andre gilt als sel’ger Sohn des Himmels.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins, may the golden-coloured (car of one of you), traversing at will the quarters of space, come to our dwellings; may mankind encourage the horses of the other by food, by friction, and by shouts.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Traversing at will: niceruс╕е kakuho va┼Ы─Бm anu: kakuha is an epithet of ratha, signifying best, ┼Ыreс╣гс╣нha; it may also mean the points of the horizon

Jamison Brereton

The attentive lead (horse) of you two, your sorrel, should go forth, following your will, to the (sacrificial) seats,
(as should) the two fallow bays of the other [=Indra]. They will become swollen with prizesтАФthe skittish (horses) as they (go) through the airy realms with their cries, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

nicer├║- is a hapax (though cf. c├йru- VIII.61.7). It almost surely belongs to тИЪci тАШobserve, discernтАЩ, with Debrunner (AiG II.860), despite MayrhoferтАЩs doubts (EWA s.v. c├йru-). The A┼Ыvins are themselves called n├нcetar- in nearby I.184.2.

The 2nd member r┼лpa- in pi┼Ы├бс╣Еga-r┼лpa- seems pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++, but it perhaps should have been rendered in tr., тАШwhose form is tawnyтАЩ, vel sim.

P─Бda c causes several problems, both in grammar and in interpretation. To start with the latter, any├бsya is universally taken as referring to one of the two A┼Ыvins, as the paired any├бс╕е-s of 4ab do. However, as noted in the published introduction, I think the referent of this stem has shifted. Both A┼Ыvins together are referred to in the first hemistich of 5, with the dual pronoun v─Бm. They are contrasted with a new тАЬthe otherтАЭ in c, who can only be Indra: the presence of the two fallow bays (h├бr─л) guarantees his presence, since these horses are uniquely IndraтАЩs.

The grammatical problem is the apparent number disharmony between the dual h├бr─л, if taken as the subject, and the pl. verb p─лp├бyanta; the accent of this verb is also potentially problematic. The standard interpr. construe the p─Бda in this way (cf. Geldner тАЬDie beiden Falben тАж sind тАж geschwelltтАЭ; so also Oldenberg, Witzel Got┼Н). The accent on a main cl. verb is attributed to the any├б- (тАж any├б-) construction (so Geldner, n. 5), though he expresses some concern that in fact thereтАЩs only one any├б-. While it is true that the first of two clauses in a double any├б- construction generally has an accented verb (e.g., I.164.20, II.40.4-5, VI.68.3), this is not universal (cf., e.g., VI.57.2), and it is not the case with single any├б-. But the real problem is that a plural verb should not have a dual subject. Both these difficulties can be avoided if we supply a (dual) form of тИЪgam in c, generated from the precative gamy─Бс╕е ending b, and start a new clause with p─лp├бyanta, which then owes its accent to its clause-initial position. The plural subject of this verb then includes both IndraтАЩs pair of fallow bays (c) and the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ tawny lead horse (a). (Geldner [n. 5] somewhat similarly suggests that p─лp├бyanta is pl.

because the kakuh├б- of 5a is also thought of [gedacht wird], but my suggestion allows a grammatical solution, not merely a notional one.) The adjective opening the next p─Бda would apply to all three horses and serve as a further plural specification of the group. Although the Pp. reads du. -─Б╠Б, in sandhi it can as well be pl. -─Бс╕е. The stem of this adjective is uncertain. S─Бyaс╣Зa., followed by M├╝ller, reads mathn─Б╠Б; Aufrecht, mathr─Б╠Б. This is one of the relatively few variant manuscript readings in the RV; see M├╝ller vol. I, p. 62, Aufr. vol. II, p. iv., and Oldenberg ad loc. On the basis of mathr─Б╠Бin VIII.46.23, Oldenberg opts for mathr─Б╠Б. This seems reasonable, though in terms of sense which suffix we choose matters little, since either form would most likely belong to тИЪmanth тАШchurn, stir, shakeтАЩ; used of horses, I take it to mean тАШagitated, excitable, skittishтАЩ.

I supply a participle of a verb of motion with v├н, which governs r├бj─Бс╣Гsi. The two parts of this phrase are separated by the intrusive voc. a┼Ыvin─Б. See 7b below.

Griffith

May your car-seat, down-gliding, golden-coloured, according to your wish approach our dwellings.
Men shall feed full the bay steeds of the other, and, Asvins they with roars shall stir the regions.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(One of you), the disperser (of the clouds), like Indra, the annihilator (of his foes), desirous of the oblation, proceeds (bestowing) abundant food. (Devout worshippers) cherish with (sacrificial) viands, (the faculties) of the other, for the sake of favours, which flow upon us like swelling rivers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Disperser of the clouds: ┼Ыaradv─Бn = ┼Ыaraс╣Зav─Бn, blighting, withering as leaves, or many-yeared, old, eternal, bahu-saс╣Гvatsaraс╕е; or, autumnal, with reference to one of the A┼Ыvins as the moon, ┼Ыaratk─Бlav─Бn; faculties of the other: the reference is to ekasya, of the one and anyasya, of the other

Jamison Brereton

Like a bull setting out to conquer, your (lead horse) of (many) autumns, dispatching many refreshing drinks of honey, goes forth
along the routes of the other [=Indra]. (The horses) will become swollen with prizes; (like) high, roiling rivers they have come to us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is quite parallel to vs. 5: it begins pr├б v─Бm, with a verb of motion in the 2nd p─Бda to be construed with pr├б (gamy─Бh and carati respectively); the 3rd p─Бdas are identical save for their first word, X any├бsya p─лp├бyanta v─Б╠Бjaiс╕е. I therefore construe the vs. as I did vs. 5 with тАЬlead horseтАЭ the subj. of ab, Indra the referent of any├бsya in c, and a new clause beginning with p─лp├бyanta. That the subj. of d is plural gives support to my suggestion that 5d also contains a plural not a dual.

┼Ыar├бdvant- тАШhaving autumns/yearsтАЩ in p─Бda a is a hapax, but presumably means тАШhaving (many) yearsтАЩ – thus тАШexperiencedтАЩ, of the lead horse.

As was noted ad I.178.2, I do not believe that we need a separate root тИЪviс╣г тАШsich ergiessenтАЩ for three passages, including this one; тАШtoil, laborтАЩ works for all the passages. My тАШroilтАЩ here, besides conveniently rhyming with тАШtoilтАЩ, is meant to express the physical motion of the waters at work.

Griffith

Forth comes your strong Bull like a cloud of autumn, sending abundant food of liquid sweetness.
Let them feed with the other’s ways and vigour: the upper streams have come and do us service.

Geldner

Euer bejahrter, wie ein Stier ├╝berlegener Buckelochse wandelt viele Labetr├дnke der S├╝├Яigkeit entsendend. Die Falben des anderen sind von den L├дufen und Siegestroph├дen geschwellt; wie die eilenden Str├╢me sind sie aufrecht zu uns gekommen.

Grassmann

Von euch der eine wie ein Bull gewaltig, eilt hin, ausspritzend viele s├╝sse Tr├дnke, Des andern Rosspaar wird von Speise schwellen, uns sind genaht die hohen Str├╢me sprudelnd.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins, creators, the perpetual threefold hymn addressed to you, has been uttered, (to secure) your steady (favour); thus glorified protect him who solicits (your bounty), and whether moving or resting, hear his invocation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

A substantial song has been sent surging to you, flowing in three parts to the plumped-up (ritual grass?), o ritual experts, A┼Ыvins.
When you are approached with praise, help the man in need; whether on your journey or not, hear my summons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand why the song would be flowing тАШin three partsтАЩ (/тАЩthreefoldтАЩ; tredh├б), nor is the meaning and referent of loc. b─Бс╕╖h├й clear. But comparison with tribarh├нс╣гi s├бdasi тАЬon the seat with three (layers) of barhisтАЭ in the next vs., 8b, may help. Assuming b─Бс╕╖h├б- belongs to тИЪbaс╣Гh тАШbe/make thick, firmтАЩ, we can assign b─Бс╕╖h├б- the sense тАШthickened, plumped upтАЩ and suggest that b─Бс╕╖h├й refers to the barhis, which has been plumped up invitingly, like a sofa cushion, for the gods to sit on, with its three layers ensuring a soft seat. As for tredh─Б╠БI now think it qualifies not the song, as in the published translation, but the seat, and would now tr. тАЬтАж flowing to the (ritual grass) plumped up threefold/in three parts.тАЭ As in 5d the two parts of this phrase b─Бс╕╖h├й tredh─Б╠Бare separated by the intrusive voc. a┼Ыvin─Б.

Thus lauded, give the suppliant protection moving or resting hear mine invocation.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the praise of your resplendent forms, (uttered) in the hall of sacrifice, thrice strewn with sacred grass, bring prosperity to the conductors (of the sacrifice). Showerers (of benefits), may the raining-cloud, proceeding to man, nourish him lik a a sprinkling of water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And this very song of the gleaming wasp [=sacrificial fire] swells in the seat of men, which has three layers of ritual grass.
O bulls, the bullish cloud [=soma] is swollen as if at the insemination of a cow [/at the pouring out of the cow (=milk)], showing favor to the sons of Manu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The gen. phrase r├║┼Ыato v├бpsasaс╕е is standardly taken as the PN (Ru┼Ыant Vapsas) of the singer. As often when a PN explanation is offered, this is a convenient way of evading an unclear word or phrase. But r├║┼Ыant- is a very well-attested adj.

with a clear sense тАШgleaming, brightтАЩ and does not otherwise form part of a PN. This leaves v├бpsas-, which I take as тАШwaspтАЩ both here and in VIII.45.5 (gir─Б╠Бv├бpso, which I divide as gir─Б╠Бv├бpso, contra Pp.; see disc. in EWA s.v. v├бpsas-). The resultant тАЬgleaming waspтАЭ is, in my opinion, a description of fire; r├║┼Ыant- is not infrequently a descriptor of fire, and тАШwaspтАЩ would refer to the random movements of flames and/or the тАЬstingтАЭ produced by flying sparks hitting skin. At least acdg. to the internet, one of the most common species of wasp in South Asia is Ropalidia marginata (often called the Indian wasp), a type of paper wasp that is remarkably flame-red in color, and, in YouTube videos, a cluster of such wasps on top of their nest looks rather like a flickering fire. Its sting is quite painful. Its тАЬsongтАЭ in this passage would either be the sound of the crackling fire compared to the buzzing of the wasps or else simply the hymn recited at the ritual fire.

The published translation careless omits the v─Бm; I would emend the tr. to тАЬthis very song тАж swells for you тАжтАЭ The second hemistich concerns the soma, in my view, though Geldner and Renou both take the bullish cloud as an image of generosity and Witzel Got┼Н as morning mist. I take this phrase as referring to the soma swollen with water after its soaking; this image is then given both a real-world and a ritual sense, playing on two senses of g├│r n├б s├йke.

In the real-world image the bull is depicted as sexually aroused (swollen) in mating with a cow, lit. тАЬat the insemination of a cow.тАЭ The root тИЪsic frequently takes r├йtas- тАШsemenтАЩ as obj., and this is a shorthand way of expressing тАЬat the pouring out (of semen) into a cow,тАЭ vel sim. But in the ritual image, тАЬat the pouring out of the cowтАЭ refers to the pouring of milk and its mixing with the soma, a very common image that is regularly sexualized.

This song of bright contents for you is swelling in the men’s hall where three-fold grass is ready.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рдкреБрд░рдВрдзрд┐рдГ рдмрд╣реБрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдГ рдкреВрд╖реЗрд╡ рдкреЛрд╖рдХ рдЗрд╡ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ рдЬрд░рддреЗ рд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдкреБрд░рдВрдзрд┐рд░реНрдмрд╣реВрдирд╛рдВ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрд┐рддреНрд░реА рдкреВрд╖реЗрд╡ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрд╡ рее рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛ рее рддрд╛рдВ рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН ред рдХрд┐рдорд┐рд╡ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореБрд╖рд╛рдВ рди ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореБрд╖рд╕рдВ рдЪ рдпрдерд╛ рддрдерд╛ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдордкрд┐ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрдГ рдЖрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирдХреНрд░рддреБрд╡рддреН рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпреЛрд╖рд╕реНрдпрдпреЛрд░рдкрд┐ рд╕рджреНрднрд╛рд╡рд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдХрджреЗрддрд┐ рдЖрд╣ ред рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рд╡рд░рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд░рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдпрдпрд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░реНрдпрдпрд╛ рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛ рд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ рддрджрд╛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рдЬрд░рддреЗ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдореЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдЧрддрдореН рее реереирейрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe wise offerer of oblations, like P┼лс╣гan, praises you, A┼Ыvins, as (he would praise) Agni and Uс╣г─Б, (at the season) at which I invoke you praising with devotion that we may thence obtain food, strength, and long life.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

At the season: the allusion is to the time at which it is especially proper to worship A┼Ыvins, the morning sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

Just as P┼лс╣гan and Plenitude (summoned) you, o A┼ЫvinsтАФthe one with the oblation sings (to you, as if) to Agni, as if to Dawn,
when I summon you, singing to you, with a longing for wide space.
тАУ May we know refreshment and a community having lively waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. seems to be trying to aggregate as many divinities into the final summons as possible, and it does so rather awkwardly. On the basis of I.117.19 ├бth─Б yuv─Б╠Бm ├нd ahvayat p├║raс╣Гdhiс╕е тАЬP. called upon just you two [=A┼Ыvins],тАЭ I take p├║raс╣Гdhiс╕е here as the separate (female) figure, rather than as an qualifier of P┼лс╣гan like Geldner Also on the basis of that passage I supply тАШsummonedтАЩ (generatable from huv├й in c) rather than making this part of the b clause with the verb jarate – though very little depends on one or the other decision.

In c gс╣Ыс╣З─Бn├бс╕е must be, quite unusually, transitive: it is ordinarily passive. I think the transitive value for this medial participle was induced by its etymological relationship with transitive jarate in b, mediated by the medial participle to that pres.

stem, which also takes the singer, not the besung, as subj. See the very similar passage VI.62.1 a┼Ыv├нn─Б huve j├бram─Бс╣Зo arka├нс╕е тАЬI call upon the A┼Ыvins, singing with my chants.тАЭ

Griffith

The prudent worshipper, like Pusan, Asvins! praises you as he praises Dawn and Agni,
When, singing with devotion, he invokes you. May we find strengthening food in full abundance.

Geldner

Euch, Asvin, ruft der Opfernde, wunscherf├╝llend wie Pusan, wach, wie den Agni, wie die Usas, da ich euch preisend lade im Wunsch nach Sorgenfreiheit. - Wir m├╢chten einen gastfreien Opferb├╝ndler kennen lernen, der rasch schenkt.

Grassmann

Euch Rittern naht wie Puschan unsre Gabe, dem Agni wie dem Morgenroth der Priester, Wenn ich euch preisend rufe mit Verlangen. Gebt Labung uns und wasserreiche Fluren.

Elizarenkova

(рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдФрд░ (рдЙрд╖рд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рдд рд╡реЗрд▓рд╛ рдХреЛ (рдпрддреН) рдЬреЛ (рдкреБрд░рдиреНрдзрд┐рдГ) рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХреЛ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдФрд░ (рдкреВрд╖реЗрд╡) рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрдд рджрд╛рди рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рди рд╡рд╣ рдЬрди (рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдореН) рддреБрдо рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ рдХреА (рди) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рдЬрд░рддреЗ) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рд╡рд╛рдореН) рддреБрдо рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ рдХреА (рд╡рд░рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛) рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдореЗрдВ рд╣реБрдП рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХреА (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рд╡рд╣ рдореИрдВ рддреБрдордХреЛ (рд╣реБрд╡реЗ) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реВрдБ рдРрд╕реЗ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди (рд╡реГрдЬрдирдореН) рдмрд▓ рдФрд░ (рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдореН) рджреАрд░реНрдШрдЬреАрд╡рди рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо) рдЬрд╛рдиреЗрдВ рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рд╕рдмрдХреА рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рдд рд╕рдордп рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд рджрд╛рдирд╢реАрд▓ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд╣рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рее реп реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐ рдХреЗ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрдд рд╕реЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдФрд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдордЭрдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдПрдХрд╕реМ рдЗрдХреНрдпрд╛рд╕реАрд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЫрдмреНрдмреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдореБрд╖рд╛рдВ рдпрддреН рдкреБрд░рдиреНрдзрд┐рдГ рдкреВрд╖реЗрд╡ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рди рдЬрд░рддреЗ рддрдерд╛ рд╡рд╛рдВ рд╡рд░рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛ рд╕ рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ рд╕рдиреНрдирд╣рдВ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╣реБрд╡реЗред рдПрд╡рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдорд┐рд╖рдВ рд╡реГрдЬрдирдВ рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдЮреНрдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдореН) (рдкреВрд╖реЗрд╡) рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдЗрд╡ (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛) рд╕рддреНрдпреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд░рдХреНрд╖рдпрд┐рддрдГ (рдкреБрд░рдиреНрдзрд┐рдГ) рдпрдГ рдкреБрд░рдВ рдЬрдЧрджреНрдзрд░рддрд┐ рд╕рдГ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН) рдкрд╛рд╡рдХрдореН (рдЙрд╖рд╛рдореН) рдЙрд╖рд╕рдВ рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рддрд╡реЗрд▓рд╛рдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдЬрд░рддреЗ) рд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ (рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╣рд╡реАрдВрд╖рд┐ рджрд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдГ (рд╣реБрд╡реЗ) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд░реЛрдорд┐ (рдпрддреН) рдпрдГ (рд╡рд╛рдореН) рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ (рд╡рд░рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛) рд╡рд░рд┐рд╡рд╕рд┐ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рднрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реЗрд╡рдирдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреН (рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдпрд╛рдореН (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН (рд╡реГрдЬрдирдореН) рдмрд▓рдореН (рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдореН) рджреАрд░реНрдШрдВ рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореН рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХрд░реЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рддрдХрд╛рд▓рдВ рдЪрд╛рд╡рд┐рдГ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрджрд╛рдирд╢реАрд▓рдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╛рдирд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ рее реп реердЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддреЗрдирд╛рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реердЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рд╢реАрддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖рдбреНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее
